It is an oyster field, and there is no charming scenery. It's a sea of no memory
2. 3. The most prominent gap between star-rated hotels in foreign countries, Hong Kong and Macao, and ordinary star-rated hotels in the mainland: the mainland lacks sensitivity and management efforts in the management of noise caused by man-made hotel corridors, making the corridors of guest rooms on each floor a free chat for room staff , A hotbed of unbridled homework making noise (it is a nigh**are for guests); the noise management of the guest room corridor should be managed 24 hours a day instead of the normal day and night schedule. Because travelers usually turn day and night upside down in order to improve efficiency, in the post-epidemic era, with the rarity of each journey, it is believed that 24-hour coverage of guest room noise has become more important. This hotel isn't particularly bad, but it doesn't and doesn't do well.
4. From the breakfast restaurant service staff to the kitchen staff, my overall evaluation is mid-to-lower. All superficial efforts have been done, with a wide variety and compatibility between Chinese and Western. Except for western dim sum, which is delicate, diverse and delicious, none of the other Chinese food is impressive. In fact, in star-rated hotels in China, the role of Chinese food that makes guests have a good reputation is particularly important in the buffet breakfast. Especially for foreign friends on business trips and domestic business people who are too tight to arrange a delicious meal.
5. In addition to meeting the requirements for comprehensive services, star hotels need to have a good and enjoyable experience of the hotel, which is different from other similar hotels. Otherwise, what criteria do guests use to choose a hotel for staying or staying multiple times? The factors that affect these standards are usually human factors. Once formed, how to form a sustainable development management model.
